</font></b><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Regulation S-T Rule&nbsp;101(b)(7)&nbsp;only
permits the submission in paper of a Form&nbsp;6-K if submitted to furnish a
report or other document that the registrant foreign private issuer must
furnish and make public under the laws of the jurisdiction in which the
registrant is incorporated, domiciled or legally organized (the registrant&#146;s &#147;home
country&#148;), or under the rules&nbsp;of the home country exchange on which the
registrant&#146;s securities are traded, as long as the report or other document is
not a press release, is not required to be and has not been distributed to the
registrant&#146;s security holders, and, if discussing a material event, has already
been the subject of a Form&nbsp;6-K submission or other Commission filing on
EDGAR.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:255.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">(All
amounts expressed in U.S. dollars unless otherwise noted)</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">AGNICO-EAGLE REPORTS Q2 2009 RESULTS;<br>
RECORD QUARTERLY GOLD PRODUCTION;</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">COMMERCIAL PRODUCTION ACHIEVED AT LAPA AND KITTILA
MINES;</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">EXPANSION PROJECTS APPROVED AT GOLDEX AND PINOS ALTOS</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Toronto
(July&nbsp;29, 2009) &#150; Agnico-Eagle Mines Limited</font></b><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">  </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(&#147;Agnico-Eagle&#148; or the &#147;Company&#148;) today reported quarterly
net income of $1.2 million, or $0.01 per share, for the second quarter of
2009.&#160; This result includes a non-cash
foreign currency translation loss of $16.7 million, or $0.12 per share, as well
as a stock option expense of $5.0 million, or $0.03 per share.&#160; In the second quarter of 2008, the Company reported
net income of $8.3 million, or $0.06 per share.&#160;
Excluding these non-cash items, net income increased significantly when
compared to the second quarter of 2008 due to a large increase in gold revenue.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Cash provided by operating activities in
the second quarter of 2009 was $26.4 million, down from cash provided by
operating activities of $92.8 million in the second quarter of 2008. The impact
of significantly higher gold production, compared to the second quarter of
2008, was more than offset by changes in working capital largely related to a
build-up of gold in inventory.&#160; Excluding
the large changes in working capital movements, cash provided by operating
activities increased significantly when compared to the second quarter of 2008
due to the large growth in gold revenue.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#147;Agnico-Eagle&#146;s production growth
continues as second quarter gold production increased 76% over the second
quarter of 2008.&#160; Both the Kittila and
Lapa mines achieved commercial production, while heap leach gold production at
the Pinos Altos mine has commenced.&#160;
Furthermore, our Meadowbank project continues to remain on schedule for
Q1 2010 start up.&#148;, said Sean Boyd, Vice-Chairman and Chief Executive
Officer.&#160; &#147;As we optimize our existing
asset base we have approved expansions at the Goldex and Pinos Altos
mines.&#160; Agnico-Eagle remains one of the
most compelling growth stories in the gold business.&#160; Additionally, over the next several quarters
we expect to release the results of two more expansion studies, at Meadowbank
and Kittila, further adding to our production growth beyond 2010&#148;, added Mr.&nbsp;Boyd.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Second quarter 2009 highlights include:</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Record Production</font></b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"> &#150; record gold production of 119,053
ounces.&#160; First gold poured at Pinos Altos
in July</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Good Cost Performance</font></b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"> &#150; LaRonde, Goldex and Lapa achieve good
minesite cost performance</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Commercial Production At Lapa And
Kittila </font></b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#150;
commercial production achieved as of May&nbsp;1 at both mines</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Remaining Two New Gold Mines On
Schedule</font></b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">
&#150; Pinos Altos and Meadowbank remain on schedule for initial production in third
quarter 2009 and first quarter 2010, respectively</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Growth profile bolstered </font></b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#150; expected after-tax internal rate of
return (&#147;IRR&#148;) of 76% at Goldex expansion and 17% at Pinos Altos expansion at
Creston Mascota</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Payable gold production(1)&nbsp;in the
second quarter of 2009 was a record 119,053 ounces at total cash costs per
ounce(2)&nbsp;of $326.&nbsp; This compares with gold production of 67,757
ounces in the second quarter of 2008 at total cash costs per ounce of $113.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The increase in production, relative to
the second quarter of 2008, is attributable to payable production from the
Goldex, Lapa and Kittila mines, which were not in commercial production in that
quarter.&#160; The mill recovery rates at the
Kittila mine have been increasing, resulting in commercial production being
achieved in May.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For the first six months of 2009,
Agnico-Eagle recorded net income of $55.6 million, or $0.36 per share, up from
the $37.3 million, or $0.26 per share, recorded in the first half of 2008.&#160; The increase in net income is primarily due
to 78% higher gold production in 2009 due to the opening of new mines, somewhat
offset by lower byproduct prices for zinc, silver and copper.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For the first six months of 2009,
Agnico-Eagle generated cash provided by operating activities of $75.2 million,
down from $146.6 million in the first half of 2008.&#160; The decrease was largely due to changes in
working capital related to the build-up of gold in inventory.&#160; Excluding these working capital changes, cash
provided by operating activities increased when compared to the first half of
2008 due to increased gold revenues, offset partly by lower byproduct revenue.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Payable gold production in the first half
of 2009 was a record 210,864 ounces, up 78% from 118,649 in the first six
months of 2008.&#160; The increase was due to
the start-up of the new Goldex, Kittila and Lapa mines.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Full year production guidance remains
unchanged at 550,000 ounces to 575,000 ounces of gold.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Conference Call&#160; Tomorrow</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company will host its quarterly
conference call on Thursday, July&nbsp;30, 2009 at 11:00&nbsp;a.m.
(E.D.T.).&#160; Management will review the
Company&#146;s financial results for the second quarter 2009 and provide an update
of its exploration and development activities.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 14.2pt;text-align:left;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Via
Webcast:</font></i></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 14.2pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A live audio webcast of the call will be available on
the Company&#146;s website homepage&nbsp;at <b><i style="font-weight:bold;">www.agnico-eagle.com.</i></b></font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 14.2pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="1" width="25%" noshade color="black" align="left"></div>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(1)&nbsp;Payable production of a mineral
means the quantity of mineral produced during a period contained in products
that are sold by the Company, whether such products are sold during the period
or held as inventory at the end of the period.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(2)&nbsp;Total cash costs per ounce is a
non-GAAP measure.&#160; For reconciliation of
this measure to production costs, as reported in the financial statements, see
Note 1 to the financial statements at the end of this news release.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 14.2pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Strong Financial
Position Maintained</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Cash and cash equivalents decreased to
$173.9 million at June&nbsp;30, 2009 from the March&nbsp;31, 2009 balance of
$208.4 million.&#160; Long term debt is $485
million at June&nbsp;30, 2009, up from $415 million at March&nbsp;31, 2009.&#160; During the second quarter, the Company
replaced a pre-existing US$300 million credit line, maturing September&nbsp;2010,
with a new non-amortizing US$600 million revolving credit facility, maturing June&nbsp;2012.&#160; As a result, the Company now has US$900
million of credit lines, of which $396 million was available at June&nbsp;30,
2009.&#160; In addition, the Company signed an
unsecured C$95 million bonding facility with Export Development Canada, which
will be used to provide letters of credit relating to the reclamation of the
Meadowbank project.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Capital expenditures in the quarter were
$155 million, including $60 million at Meadowbank, $43 million at Pinos Altos,
$24 million at Kittila, $19 million at LaRonde, $7 million at Lapa and $2
million at Goldex.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In 2009, full year capital expenditures
are expected to total approximately $550 million, up $10 million from previous
guidance, reflecting new expansion expenditures at Goldex.&#160; An additional $64 million will be invested
for the Creston Mascota expansion in 2010.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">LaRonde Mine &#150; Continued Cost
Control and Production Consistency</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
100% owned LaRonde mine in northwestern Quebec, Canada, began operation in
1988.&#160; Overall, proven and probable gold
reserves at LaRonde total approximately 5.0 million ounces from 35.8 million
tonnes grading 4.3 grams per tonne (&#147;g/t&#148;).&#160;
Life of mine average gold production is expected to be approximately
320,000 ounces per year through 2022.&#160;
First production from the new internal shaft of the LaRonde Extension
remains on schedule for late 2011.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The LaRonde mill processed an average of
7,212 tonnes of ore per day in the second quarter of 2009, compared with an
average of 7,281 tonnes per day in the prior-year period.&#160; With a steady-state operation of approximately
7,200 tonnes per day for approximately six years, LaRonde continues to be a
consistent, reliable world class mine.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net of byproduct credits, LaRonde&#146;s total
cash costs per ounce were $109 in the second quarter on production of 58,034
ounces of gold.&#160; This compares with the
results of the</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">3</font></p>

<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">second quarter of 2008 when total cash
costs per ounce were $113 on production of 59,452 ounces of gold.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For the first six months of 2009, LaRonde&#146;s
total cash costs per ounce were $196 on gold production of 109,372 ounces, as
compared to the first half of 2008, when the total cash cost per ounce were <i>minus $123 </i>on<i>  </i>production of
110,344 ounces of gold<i>.&#160; </i>The year-over-year increase in
total cash costs is primarily due to the significantly lower realized prices of
byproduct metals. The realized prices for silver, zinc and copper for six
months ending June&nbsp;30, 2009 were 24%, 34% and 46% lower, respectively,
compared to the first half of 2008.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Minesite costs per tonne(3)&nbsp;were
approximately C$74 in the second quarter, as expected, compared to C$68 in the
second quarter of 2008.&#160; On a
year-to-date basis, 2009 minesite costs per tonne were C$73, which compares to
C$66 in the first half of 2008.&#160; These
costs are higher than the comparable periods in 2008 due to ore stockpile
adjustments and the impact of general cost inflation.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">LaRonde Extension &#150; Shaft Sinking
Nearly Complete</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During the second quarter of 2009,
approximately 120 metres of shaft sinking was completed on the new internal
shaft, leaving approximately 120 metres to the final depth of 2,880
metres.&#160; The shaft is expected to be
completed during the fourth quarter of 2009 with preproduction development
starting thereafter.&#160; The project is on
schedule to start production in late 2011.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Goldex Mine &#150; Reaches Design
Capacity</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The 100% owned Goldex mine in
northwestern Quebec began operation in 2008.&#160;
Proven and probable gold reserves total 1.6 million ounces from 23.8
million tonnes grading 2.1 g/t.&#160; Life of
mine average annual gold production is expected to be approximately 160,000
ounces per year through 2017.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Goldex mine has successfully reached
the design capacity for the plant in the second quarter of 2009, with an
average of 6,875 tonnes of ore milled daily.&#160;
In the first quarter of 2009, the mill processed an average of 6,770
tonnes per day.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Second quarter 2009 gold production at
Goldex was 35,645 ounces at total cash costs per ounce of $365.&#160; This compares with 35,959 ounces at total
cash costs per ounce of $338 in first quarter of 2009.&#160; The higher cash cost per ounce was due to an
expected decrease in grade during the second quarter.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For the six month period ending June&nbsp;30,
2009, total cash costs at Goldex were $352 per ounce on gold production of
71,604 ounces.&#160; There is no meaningful
comparable prior year period, as Goldex achieved commercial production in August&nbsp;2008.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Cost control was very good at Goldex as
minesite costs per tonne were C$24 in the second quarter, compared to C$25 in
the first quarter of 2009.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><hr size="1" width="25%" noshade color="black" align="left"></div>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(3)&nbsp;Minesite costs per tonne is a
non-GAAP measure.&#160; For reconciliation of
this measure to production costs, as reported in the financial statements, see
Note 1 to the financial statements at the end of this news release.</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During the second quarter of 2009,
approximately 1.1 million tonnes of ore were blasted at Goldex compared with
approximately 677,000 tonnes hoisted.&#160;
This difference is necessary as the mining method used at Goldex requires
some of the broken ore to be temporarily left within the mining block as ground
support.&#160; As a result, minesite costs per
tonne are expected to decrease going forward as all production blasting is
expected to be completed in 2012, while the anticipated mine life extends into
2017.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Goldex Expansion &#150; Low Capital,
High Return Project</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Board of Directors has approved the expansion of Goldex to 8,000 tonnes per day
with the ramp-up to this higher rate expected to be achieved by late-2011.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Capital
costs are expected to total approximately $10 million, providing an internal
rate of return of&#160; approximately 76% at
$780 per ounce for gold and a C$/US$ exchange rate of 1.10.&#160; Annual incremental gold production is expected
to be approximately 20,000 ounces per year, over a mine life into 2017.&#160; As a result, total gold production at Goldex
is expected to be approximately 173,000 ounces per year beginning in 2011.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
large majority of the capital is to be spent on a surface crushing plant, with
minor amounts for modifications to ore conveyance.&#160; Detailed engineering is underway and
construction of the project will begin in the fourth quarter of 2009.&#160; A certificate of authorization, and all
necessary permits, were received to increase the production rate at Goldex from
6,900 tonnes per day up to 8,500 tonnes per day.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
spite of the increased mining rate, Agnico-Eagle expects to extend the mine
life of Goldex.&#160; There are several nearby
zones underground, on the Goldex property, that are likely to be mined.&#160; They are currently in the resource category
and not included in reserves.&#160; For
example, it is expected that the nearby &#147;M&#148; zone will contribute approximately
250,000 ounces of gold to the overall reserves at Goldex by year end 2009, thus
increasing the mine life in spite of the higher production rate.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Kittila Mine &#150; Commercial
Production Achieved at May&nbsp;1; Ramping Up Production To Design Parameters</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The 100% owned Kittila mine in northern
Finland poured its first gold in January&nbsp;2009.&#160; Proven and probable gold reserves total 3.2
million ounces from 21.4 million tonnes grading 4.7 g/t.&#160; Life of mine average gold production is
expected to be approximately 150,000 ounces per year through 2023.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During the second quarter of 2009, the
Kittila mill achieved commercial production and processed an average of 1,980
tonnes per day, reflecting the start-up phase of the project.&#160; In June&nbsp;the mill processed an average of
approximately 2,300 tonnes per day.&#160; This
compares to the expected full production rate of 3,000 tonnes per day.&#160; The current performance improvements are in
line with the Company&#146;s expectations.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Second quarter 2009 gold production at
Kittila was 13,771 ounces at total cash costs per ounce of $658.&#160; These costs are expected to decline as the
mine continues to ramp up towards full production capacity and the mill
achieves higher recoveries.&#160; Life of mine</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">5</font></p>

<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">total cash costs per ounce are expected
to be approximately $350 per ounce.&#160;
Minesite costs per tonne at Kittila were approximately &#128;43 in the second
quarter.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During the second quarter, operations at
Kittila were focused on improving gold recovery through a metallurgical
optimization process aimed to achieve Kittila&#146;s design gold recoveries of 83%
to 89% in the mill, over the life of the mine. The optimization process has
delivered significant results to date, with mill recoveries averaging 49% in
the second quarter and 65% in June, both much higher than the average of 28%
realized in the first quarter of 2009.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A
scoping study is underway examining the possibility of significantly increasing
the designed production rate at Kittila.&#160;
This plan involves sinking a shaft on the property combined with an
increase in milling capacity.&#160; Results of
the study are expected to be released later this year and will incorporate the
most recent exploration drilling.&#160; Eleven
drills, two underground and nine on surface, are currently working on resource
to reserve conversion and other exploration around the current reserves.&#160; Year to date, over 46,200 metres of diamond
drilling has been completed at Kittila while an additional 14,600 metres of
drilling has been completed on regional exploration in Finland.&#160; Results will be presented in an upcoming
exploration update.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Lapa &#150; Commercial
Production Achieved at May&nbsp;1; Production Nearing Design Parameters</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The 100% owned Lapa mine in northwestern
Quebec began production in April&nbsp;2009.&#160;
Proven and probable gold reserves total 1.1 million ounces from 3.8
million tonnes grading 8.8 g/t.&#160; Life of
mine average gold production is expected to be approximately 115,000 ounces per
year through 2015.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On May&nbsp;1, Lapa achieved
commercial production.&#160; Production from
the Lapa mine (all of which is processed at the LaRonde mill), has averaged
1,270 tonnes per day in June, which is progressing towards design
parameters.&#160;&#160; The expected production
rate over the life of the mine is 1,500 tonnes per day.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Second quarter 2009 gold production at
Lapa was 11,603 ounces at total cash costs per ounce of $948, partly reflecting
the mine and mill start-up where some low grade development ore was mixed with
higher grade stope ore and used to commission the mill.&#160; These costs are expected to decline as the
mine continues to ramp up towards full production capacity and the drilling,
blasting, excavation and filling cycle are optimized for the orebody.&#160; Over the life of the mine, total cash costs
per ounce are expected to average approximately $315.&#160; Minesite costs per tonne at Lapa were
approximately C$149 in the second quarter, reflecting the start-up phase of the
mine.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="background:white;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">To
date, nine of the 750 stopes expected to be extracted over the mine life have
been removed.&#160; Reconciliation with the
mill is expected to be completed during the third quarter once more consistent
feed is delivered to it.&#160; Dilution has
initially been higher than plan, however, improvements are expected as the mine
and its operations are optimized.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="background:white;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="background:white;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">6</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p style="background:white;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="background:white;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Pinos Altos Construction
Progressing On Schedule &#150; Pours First Gold from Heap Leach</font></b></p>

<p style="background:white;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The 100% owned Pinos Altos mine in
northern Mexico has begun to pour gold from the heap leach and is expected to
begin production from its milling operation in the third quarter of 2009.&#160; Proven and probable gold reserves total 3.6
million ounces and 100 million ounces of silver from 41.8 million tonnes
grading 2.7 g/t of gold and 74.6 g/t silver.&#160;
Life of mine average gold production is expected to be approximately
170,000 ounces per year through 2028, including production from Creston
Mascota.&#160; Over this period, annual silver
production is expected to average 2.5 million ounces.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
first ore was placed on the leach pads during May&nbsp;2009 and the first gold
bar was poured in July.&#160; Once the project
is in full operation, heap leaching of low grade ores is expected to contribute
approximately 5-10% of the total planned gold production from Pinos Altos.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Construction
of the mill at Pinos Altos is 90% complete and commissioning of the milling
circuit is in progress.&#160; Open pit
stripping continued at better than planned rate with 5.1 million tonnes mined,
including stripping at the Oberon de Weber pit.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Underground
development productivity remains better than anticipated.&#160; Connection of the main production ramp and
the exploration ramp is expected sometime during the third quarter, after which
time, development of initial mining levels is expected to commence.&#160; Project to date development is now nearly
seven kilometres in total.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Approximately
37,000 metres of diamond drilling were completed at the Pinos Altos mine site
and on property-wide exploration in the first half of 2009.&#160; Two surface and two underground diamond
drills were testing deep mine exploration targets at Santo Nino and Cerro
Colorado and expanding the resource on strike and at depth at San Eligio.&#160; Outside the mine-site,&#160; three other drills were exploring the main
northern Reyna de Plata structure at El Sinter, testing the Cubiro gold showing
in the western portion of the property, and exploring for extensions of the
Creston Mascota deposit.&#160; Results will be
presented in an upcoming exploration update.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Creston Mascota Approved for Construction &#150; First gold expected early
2011</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Company is about to begin construction of a stand-alone open pit, heap leach
operation on the Creston Mascota deposit, approximately 10 kilometres to the
northwest of the main Santo Nino deposit at Pinos Altos.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Probable
reserves at Creston Mascota total approximately 6.7 million tonnes grading 1.65
g/t gold and 17.1 g/t silver, or approximately 357,000 ounces of gold and 3.7
million ounces of silver.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
recently reviewed feasibility study contemplates a 4,000 tonne per day
operation with first production in early 2011.&#160;
Gold recoveries of 65% and silver recoveries of 16% are assumed for the
heap leach operation planned at Creston Mascota.&#160; The waste to ore stripping ratio is expected
to be approximately 4:1.&#160; Minesite costs
per tonne are </font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">7</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

</div>
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='7',FILE='C:\JMS\105935\09-20165-1\task3650576\20165-1-ka-01.htm',USER='105935',CD='Jul 30 20:09 2009' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">assumed
to be approximately $13.&#160; Total cash
costs are expected to be $340 per ounce of gold.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Capital
costs are expected to total approximately $64 million, providing an internal
rate of return of&#160; approximately 17% at
$780 per ounce for gold and $13.70 per ounce for silver.&#160; Annual gold production is expected to be
approximately 46,000 ounces per year, over a five year mine life.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Construction
on the project will begin in the fourth quarter of 2009 and is expected to take
approximately 18 months to complete.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Separately,
the Company is studying the possibility of increasing the milled production
rate at the main Pinos Altos deposits from 4,000 tonnes per day to 6,000 tonnes
per day, reflecting the 125% increase in reserve tonnage since 2007.&#160; Results of the scoping study are expected by
the third quarter of 2010.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Meadowbank Project Remains
on Schedule for Q1, 2010 Start-Up</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The 100% owned Meadowbank mine project in
Nunavut, northern Canada, is expected to begin production in the first quarter
of 2010.&#160; Probable gold reserves total
3.6 million ounces from 32.8 million tonnes grading 3.5 g/t.&#160; Life of mine average annual gold production
is expected to be approximately 350,000 ounces through 2019.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Construction
of the new Meadowbank mine project is well advanced.&#160; Highlights include the completion of the
semi-autogenous (&#147;SAG&#148;) and ball mill foundations and the installation of the
SAG mill.&#160; Two thickeners and the cyanide
destruction tank have been completed.&#160;
The dewatering of Second Portage Lake Phase One has been finished.&#160; The balance will be completed upon the
delivery of the water treatment plant expected this summer.&#160; Two of the six generators were installed in
the power plant.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
2009 sea-lift season is underway, including the remaining materials and
consumables required for project completion.&#160;
All of the major equipment for the various milling circuits is already
in place.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Pre-stripping
in the Portage pit is underway with approximately 2.0 million tonnes of waste
rock hauled during the first half of 2009.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
the first half of 2009, approximately 27,400 metres of exploration drilling was
completed at the Meadowbank minesite in the winter program.&#160; Four drills were dedicated to the mining area
between Portage and Goose zones and also at depth.&#160; An additional 20,500 metres were completed on
exploration targets on the surrounding Meadowbank property, using three
drills.&#160; The targets included the Vault
deposit, located approximately 10 kilometres to the north.&#160; Results will be presented in an upcoming
exploration update.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A
scoping study is underway which is considering an increase in the average daily
production rate from 8,500 tonnes per day to 10,000 tonnes per day.&#160; This would increase the average annual gold
production to more than 400,000 ounces.&#160;
Results of the study are expected in the third quarter of 2009, with
review in the fourth quarter.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">8</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
<div>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">About Agnico-Eagle</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Agnico-Eagle is a long established,
Canadian headquartered, gold producer with operations located in Canada,
Finland and Mexico, and exploration and development activities in Canada,
Finland, Mexico and the United States.&#160;
Agnico-Eagle&#146;s LaRonde mine is Canada&#146;s largest operating gold mine in
terms of reserves.&#160; The Company has full
exposure to higher gold prices consistent with its policy of no forward gold
sales.&#160; It has paid a cash dividend for
27 consecutive years.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">9</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p style="margin:0in 50.95pt .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 50.95pt .0001pt .5in;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Note 1</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 50.95pt .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 50.95pt .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Lapa achieved commercial production as of May&nbsp;1, 2009.&#160; Payable production includes commercial
production ounces of 11,603 since May&nbsp;1, 2009; non-commercial production
ounces were nil.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 50.95pt .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 50.95pt .0001pt .5in;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Note 2</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 50.95pt .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 50.95pt .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kittila achieved commercial production as of May&nbsp;1, 2009.&#160; Payable production includes commercial
production ounces of 12,018 since May&nbsp;1, 2009.&#160; Non-commercial production was 1,753 ounces.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 50.95pt .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 50.95pt .0001pt .5in;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Note 3</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 50.95pt .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 50.95pt .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Total cash costs per ounce is calculated net of copper, zinc and other
byproduct credits. The weighted average is based on commercial production
ounces.&#160; Total cash costs per ounce is a
non-GAAP measure.&#160; For a reconciliation
to the financial statements, see Note 2 to the financial statements.&#160; See also &#147;Note Regarding Certain Measures of
Performance&#148;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">CONSOLIDATED BALANCE SHEETS</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">(thousands of United States dollars,
US GAAP basis)</font></b></p>

  <p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:1.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&nbsp;</font></b></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="1" width="25%" noshade color="black" align="left"></div>

<table border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" width="97%" style="border-collapse:collapse;width:97.86%;">
 <tr>
  <td width="6%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:6.82%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(i)</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="93%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:93.18%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Under the Company&#146;s revenue recognition policy, revenue is recognized
  on concentrates when legal title passes. Since total cash costs are
  calculated on a production basis, this inventory adjustment reflects the
  sales margin on the portion of concentrate production for which revenue has
  not been recognized in the&nbsp;period.</font></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td width="6%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:6.82%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="93%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:93.18%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td width="6%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:6.82%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(ii)</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="93%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:93.18%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Total cash costs per ounce is not a recognized measure under US GAAP
  and this data may not be comparable to data presented by other gold
  producers. The Company believes that this generally accepted industry measure
  is a realistic indication of operating performance and is useful in allowing
  year over year comparisons. As illustrated in the table above, this measure
  is calculated by adjusting Production Costs as shown in the Consolidated
  Statements of Income and Comprehensive Income for net byproduct revenues,
  royalties, inventory adjustments and asset retirement provisions. This
  measure is intended to provide investors with information about the cash
  generating capabilities of the Company&#146;s mining operations. Management uses
  this measure to monitor the performance of the Company&#146;s mining operations.
  Since market prices for gold are quoted on a per ounce basis, using this per
  ounce measure allows management to assess the mine&#146;s cash generating
  capabilities at various gold prices. Management is aware that this per ounce
  measure of performance can be impacted by fluctuations in byproduct metal
  prices and exchange rates. Management compensates for the limitation inherent
  with this measure by using it in conjunction with the minesite costs per
  tonne measure (discussed below) as well as other data prepared in accordance
  with US GAAP. Management also performs sensitivity analyses in order to
  quantify the effects of fluctuating metal prices and exchange&nbsp;rates.</font></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td width="6%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:6.82%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="93%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:93.18%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td width="6%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:6.82%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(iii)</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="93%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:93.18%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This inventory adjustment reflects production costs associated with
  unsold concentrates.</font></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td width="6%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:6.82%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="93%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:93.18%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td width="6%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:6.82%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(iv)</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="93%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:93.18%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Minesite costs per tonne is
  not a recognized measure under US GAAP and this data may not be comparable to
  data presented by other gold producers. As illustrated in the table above, this
  measure is calculated by adjusting Production Costs as shown in the
  Consolidated Statements of Income and Comprehensive Income for inventory and
  asset retirement provisions and then dividing by tonnes processed through the
  mill. Since total cash costs data can be affected by fluctuations in
  byproduct metal prices and exchange rates, management believes minesite costs
  per tonne provides additional information regarding the performance of mining
  operations and allows management to monitor operating costs on a more
  consistent basis as the per tonne measure eliminates the cost variability
  associated with varying production levels. Management also uses this measure
  to determine the economic viability of mining blocks. As each mining block is
  evaluated based on the net realizable value of each tonne mined, in order to
  be economically viable the estimated revenue on a per tonne basis must be in
  excess of the minesite costs per tonne. Management is aware that this per
  tonne measure is impacted by fluctuations in production levels and thus uses
  this evaluation tool in conjunction with production costs prepared in
  accordance with US GAAP. This measure supplements production cost information
  prepared in accordance with US GAAP and allows investors to distinguish between
  changes in production costs resulting from changes in production versus
  changes in operating performance.</font></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
</table>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">17</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Detailed Mineral Reserve and Resource Data</font></b><b><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">  </font></b><b><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">(as at December&nbsp;31,
2008)</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<table border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" width="100%" style="border-collapse:collapse;width:100.0%;">
 <tr>
  <td width="33%" valign="bottom" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:33.0%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 10.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:1.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&nbsp;</font></b></p>
  </td>
  <td width="2%" valign="bottom" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:2.5%;">
  <p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:1.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&nbsp;</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">not assume any obligation, to update

things, grade, tonnage, processing, mining methods, capital costs, total cash
costs, minesite costs, and location of surface infrastructure.&#160; Actual results and final decisions may be
materially different from those current anticipated.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Notes To Investors
Regarding The Use Of Resources</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Cautionary Note To
Investors Concerning Estimates Of Measured And Indicated Resources.</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This press
release uses the terms &#147;measured resources&#148; and &#147;indicated resources&#148;. We
advise investors that while those terms are recognized and required by Canadian
regulations, the SEC does not recognize them. <b>Investors
are cautioned not to assume that any part or all of mineral deposits in these
categories will ever be converted into reserves</b>.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Cautionary Note To
Investors Concerning Estimates Of Inferred Resources.</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This press
release also uses the term &#147;inferred resources&#148;. We advise investors that while
this term is recognized and required by Canadian regulations, the SEC does not
recognize it. &#147;Inferred resources&#148; have a great amount of uncertainty as to
their existence, and great uncertainty as to their economic and legal
feasibility. It cannot be assumed that all or any part of an inferred mineral
resource will ever be upgraded to a higher category. Under Canadian rules,
estimates of inferred mineral resources may not form the basis of feasibility
or pre-feasibility studies, except in rare cases. <b>Investors are cautioned not to assume that part or all of an inferred
resource exists, or is economically or legally mineable.</b></font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Scientific And Technical
Data</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Agnico-Eagle
Mines Limited is reporting mineral resource and reserve estimates in accordance
with the CIM guidelines for the estimation, classification and reporting of
resources and reserves.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Cautionary Note To U.S.
Investors</font></b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">  <b>-</b> The
SEC permits U.S. mining companies, in their filings with the SEC, to disclose
only those mineral deposits that a company can economically and legally extract
or produce. We use certain terms in this press release, such as &#147;measured&#148;, &#147;indicated&#148;,
and &#147;inferred&#148;, and &#147;resources&#148; that the SEC guidelines strictly prohibit U.S.
registered companies from including in their filings with the SEC. U.S.
Investors are urged to consider closely the disclosure in our Form&nbsp;20-F,
which may be obtained from us, or from the SEC&#146;s website at: </font><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">http://sec.gov/edgar.shtml.&#160; A &#147;final&#148;
or &#147;bankable&#148; feasibility study is required to meet the requirements to
designate reserves under Industry Guide 7.&#160;
Estimates were calculated using historic three-year average metals
prices and foreign exchange rates in accordance with the SEC Industry Guide
7.&#160; Industry Guide 7 requires the use of
prices that reflect current economic conditions at the time of reserve
determination which Staff of the SEC has interpreted to mean historic
three-year average prices.&#160; The
assumptions used for the mineral reserves and resources estimate reported by
the Company on February&nbsp;18th, 2009 were based on three-year average prices</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">20</font></p>

<div align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">for the period
ending December&nbsp;31, 2008&#160; of $725
per ounce&#160; gold, $13.32 per ounce silver,
$1.27 per pound zinc, $3.15 per pound copper, $0.90 per pound lead and C$/US$,
US$/Euro and MXP/US$ exchange rates of 1.09, 1.37 and 11.00, respectively.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Canadian
Securities Administrators&#146; National Instrument 43-101 (&#147;NI 43-101&#148;) requires
mining companies to disclose reserves and resources using the subcategories of &#147;proven&#148;
reserves, &#147;probable&#148; reserves, &#147;measured&#148; resources, &#147;indicated&#148; resources and &#147;inferred&#148;
resources. Mineral resources that are not mineral reserves do not have
demonstrated economic viability.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A mineral
reserve is the economically mineable part of a measured or indicated resource
demonstrated by at least a preliminary feasibility study. This study must
include adequate information on mining, processing, metallurgical, economic and
other relevant factors that demonstrate, at the time of reporting, that
economic extraction can be justified. A mineral reserve includes diluting
materials and allows for losses that may occur when the material is mined. A
proven mineral reserve is the economically mineable part of a measured resource
for which quantity, grade or quality, densities, shape and physical characteristics
are so well established that they can be estimated with confidence sufficient
to allow the appropriate application of technical and economic parameters, to
support production planning and evaluation of the economic viability of the
deposit. A probable mineral reserve is the economically mineable part of an
indicated mineral resource for which quantity, grade or quality, densities,
shape and physical characteristics can be estimated with a level of confidence
sufficient to allow the appropriate application of technical and economic
parameters, to support mine planning and evaluation of the economic viability
of the deposit.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A mineral
resource is a concentration or occurrence of natural, solid, inorganic or
fossilized organic material in or on the Earth&#146;s crust in such form and
quantity and of such a grade or quality that it has reasonable prospects for
economic extraction. The location, quantity, grade, geological characteristics
and continuity of a mineral resource are known, estimated or interpreted from
specific geological evidence and knowledge. A measured mineral resource is that
part of a mineral resource for which quantity, grade or quality, densities,
shape and physical characteristics can be estimated with a level of confidence
sufficient to allow the appropriate application of technical and economic
parameters, to support mine planning and evaluation of the economic viability
of the deposit. The estimate is based on detailed and reliable exploration,
sampling and testing information gathered through appropriate techniques from
locations such as outcrops, trenches, pits, workings and drill holes that are
spaced closely enough to confirm both geological and grade continuity. An
indicated mineral resource is that part of a mineral resource for which
quantity, grade or quality, densities, shape and physical characteristics can
be estimated with a level of confidence sufficient to allow the appropriate
application of technical and economic parameters, to support mine planning and
evaluation of the economic viability of the deposit. The estimate is based on
detailed and reliable exploration and testing information gathered through
appropriate techniques from locations such as outcrops, trenches, pits,
workings and drill holes that are spaced closely enough for geological and
grade continuity to be reasonably assumed. An inferred mineral resource is that
part of a mineral resource for which quantity and grade or quality can be
estimated on the basis of geological evidence and limited sampling and reasonably
assumed, but not verified, geological and grade continuity. The estimate is
based on limited information and sampling gathered through appropriate
techniques from locations such as outcrops, trenches, pits, workings and drill</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">21</font></p>

<div align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">holes. Mineral
resources which are not mineral reserves do not have demonstrated economic
viability.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Investors are cautioned
not to assume that part or all of an inferred resource exists, or is
economically or legally mineable.</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A feasibility
study is a comprehensive study of a mineral deposit in which all geological,
engineering, legal, operating, economic, social, environmental and other
relevant factors are considered in sufficient detail that it could reasonably
serve as the basis for a final decision by a financial institution to finance
the development of the deposit for mineral production.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The mineral
reserves presented in this disclosure are separate from and not a portion of
the mineral resources.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

projects that is required by NI 43-101, sections 3.2 and 3.3 and paragraphs 3.4
(a), (c)&nbsp;and (d)&nbsp;can be found in the Technical Reports referred to
above, which may be found at www.sedar.com. Other important operating
information can be found in the Company&#146;s press release dated December&nbsp;11,

<div>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&nbsp;</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Note Regarding Certain
Measures Of Performance</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This press
release presents measures including &#147;total cash costs per ounce&#148; and &#147;minesite
costs per tonne&#148; that are not recognized measures under US GAAP. This data may
not be comparable to data presented by other gold producers. The Company
believes that these generally accepted industry measures are realistic
indicators of operating performance and useful for year-over-year comparisons.
However, both of these non-GAAP measures should be considered together with
other data prepared in accordance with US GAAP, these measures, taken by
themselves, are not necessarily indicative of operating costs or cash flow
measures prepared in accordance with US GAAP.&#160;
The Company provides a reconciliation of realized total cash costs per
ounce and minesite costs per tonne to the most comparable US GAAP measures in
its annual and interim filings with securities regulators in Canada and the
United States.&#160; A reconciliation of the
Company&#146;s total cash costs per ounce and minesite costs per tonne to the most
comparable financial measures calculated and presented in accordance with US
GAAP for the Company&#146;s historical results of operations is set out in Note 1 to
the financial statements included herein.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
